  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1282119529">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1282119529" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1143969-julie" class="left imgcol" title="Julie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1409947508p2/1143969.jpg" alt="Julie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1282119529?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1143969-julie" class="user" title="Julie">Julie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=rereads" class="actionLinkLite">rereads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1282119529">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18387175244987200932">Ghostwriter: Ellen Geroux.<br /><br />So, speaking of Tobias and identity issues...<br /><br />I keep mentioning that the last several books have been painful, and this one is no exception. The plot actually picks up on the mission introduced in the previous book: the Yeerks are developing an Anti-Morphing Ray, and so the Animorphs decide to use Tobias as bait in order to make the Yeerks think that it doesn't work. They willingly let Tobias be captured to further their aims.<br /><br />Sacrifice and hard decisions have been the de</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18387175244987200932">Ghostwriter: Ellen Geroux.<br /><br />So, speaking of Tobias and identity issues...<br /><br />I keep mentioning that the last several books have been painful, and this one is no exception. The plot actually picks up on the mission introduced in the previous book: the Yeerks are developing an Anti-Morphing Ray, and so the Animorphs decide to use Tobias as bait in order to make the Yeerks think that it doesn't work. They willingly let Tobias be captured to further their aims.<br /><br />Sacrifice and hard decisions have been the de facto theme for a while now. Which ties into one of my favourite quotes here, which is nothing new and has been touched on before, but it really illustrates the toll of leadership:<br /><blockquote>"I'm glad you made it, Tobias. You're our eyes. Our ears. Our air force. If we lost you, we'd be nothing. Like Joan of Arc without her sword, Patton without his pearl-handled pistols..."<br /><br />&lt;Saddam without forty-eight palaces, the special Republican Guard, and a jar of anthrax? Stop the flattery, man. You’re making me blush.&gt; We both laughed. It felt good to hear Jake say I was indispensable, but with Jake you could never be sure anymore what was sincere. And what was just expedient.<br /><br />He’d been the most open of guys, back in the old days. What you saw with Jake was what you got. But he’d been a leader for a long time now. He’d learned to say what he needed to say.<br /><br />Jake needed me as one of the Animorphs. He liked me, respected me, was happy for me when I was happy. And, when he had to, he used me without regard for anything but winning.</blockquote><br />It's delivered matter-of-fact, but it's a quietly heartbreaking moment for me: the insidious creeping doubt inside these friendships, to the extent of mistrusting a simple compliment. Yet Tobias does so for good reason -- I don't think he's wrong about it, either. It's also so complicated knowing that Jake can manipulate his own friends (soldiers) for the greater good, but draws the line at his innocent family. He isn't infallible.<br /><br />Anyway. After Tobias is captured, he's on his own. This book actually reminds me a bit of #6 The Capture in that regard, in that the last chunk of the book retreats into Tobias' head and becomes an internal struggle, a mental battle, see-sawing through memories. It feels like most of the book is him being tortured at the hands of an unstable Yeerk; the section drags on, not because it's bad, but because it's excruciating. He's tortured. Emotionally, physically. Straight-up tortured.<br /><br />It's a very good book, but it does feel a bit like it's re-treading old ground; Tobias has been wrestling with his "am I human or hawk or what" feelings for over thirty books now. Which is an overly-simplified way of describing it, and I suppose kudos to the series for not neatly and easily resolving an issue like that within a single book, but I feel like I want a bit more (hence docking a star). I want more scenes like him morphing Andalite and learning about Andalite culture from Ax, exploring his own 'heritage', so to speak.<br /><br />Also, I only just recently realised that until the forties, Ax and Tobias have half as many narrated books as the others, trading off books in the narration order -- this might actually explain why Tobias was one of the characters I connected with least over the course of the series. It's a shame, because he <em>is</em> great. (Ax still stood out to me because his book was the first one I ever read, and plus, yanno, he's an alien, so I pay more attention to him.)<br /><br />The last idyllic scene of all the Animorphs relaxing at the beach together, and Tobias/Rachel being adorable, is an extremely welcome one. They've all been through a fucking lot lately, every single one of them. It's been a rough ride ever since the David trilogy, rarely letting up.<br /><br />They deserve the downtime, but I can't imagine the future books are going to be any easier on them.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18387175244987200932">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1141760388">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16136023487533255061">This is by far the darkest issue in the Animorphs series yet. The fact that it centres around Tobias kind of tells you everything, really.<br /><br />Tobias is still struggling with his identity as both a bird and a boy, when he volunteers to be the bait in a Yeerk trap. The Animorphs need to make the Yeerks think they’ve caught an Andalite, and as Tobias can easily morph and demorph from Andalite without revealing that the bandits are a bunch of kids, he’s the natural choice. Unfortunately it doesn’t go to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16136023487533255061">This is by far the darkest issue in the Animorphs series yet. The fact that it centres around Tobias kind of tells you everything, really.<br /><br />Tobias is still struggling with his identity as both a bird and a boy, when he volunteers to be the bait in a Yeerk trap. The Animorphs need to make the Yeerks think they’ve caught an Andalite, and as Tobias can easily morph and demorph from Andalite without revealing that the bandits are a bunch of kids, he’s the natural choice. Unfortunately it doesn’t go too smoothly for Tobias - he’s repeatedly tortured by a pretty blonde Controller to the brink of death, until the Animorphs come in and save the day. <br /><br />---<br /><br />Sometimes I struggle with the idea that these were books written for kids. Sure, there are sad moments in every Disney movie and that helps kids learn about death and conflict, but this was pushing it a bit for me. I was horrified and upset, seeing into his psyche as he was tortured almost to the point of insanity. Even though this is clearly a fictional series, it was a horrible reminder of some of the things that humanity is capable of. I’m happy to go back to farfetched tales about time travel to the Jurassic period. :( </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16136023487533255061">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1326359708">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1326359708" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1833384-jen" class="left imgcol" title="Jen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1233203080p2/1833384.jpg" alt="Jen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1326359708?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 05, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1833384-jen" class="user" title="Jen">Jen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1326359708">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9331622069295415887">Holy crow, you want to talk about right in the feels? On a certain level, I can't believe Scholastic had the guts/temerity to publish and market this and give it to kids. I am so incredibly glad they did, but whoa; even as an adult this rips my heart out and stomps on it.<br /><br />My one biggest beef with this would be that they carry forward the mission from the last book, but it seems absolutely no one has anything to say about Rachel being one person again. I think Applegate lost out on so much by not</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9331622069295415887">Holy crow, you want to talk about right in the feels? On a certain level, I can't believe Scholastic had the guts/temerity to publish and market this and give it to kids. I am so incredibly glad they did, but whoa; even as an adult this rips my heart out and stomps on it.<br /><br />My one biggest beef with this would be that they carry forward the mission from the last book, but it seems absolutely no one has anything to say about Rachel being one person again. I think Applegate lost out on so much by not exploring the fall-out from the two Rachels plotline, *especially* since this is a Tobias book.<br /><br />That said, this book is so incredible in that it spends a goodly chunk of its time actually describing torture. In a YA book. That's something else, and to have a character as awesome as Tobias have to explore what it is to stay yourself under the most extreme circumstances was outrageously intense. I can't...I just...I was totally with Rachel when she wanted to rip Taylor apart, even though I know Tobias was right.<br /><br />In this we get to see that Jake is drawing further and further into leader mode, which is a whole different kind of heartbreaking; we get to see a voluntary host and how humanity is itself crap sometimes and doesn't need Yeerks to create bad situations; and we get to add the Andalite heritage Tobias has to his identity crisis. I like that that is pressed so much here, since we know that Elfangor is Tobias's dad and since the boy/bird paradox is wearing a little thin by now. Tossing in the Andalite variable really brings a new dimension to Tobias trying to figure himself out, and I love love love his morphing Ax and being able to tell us what the raw nature of an Andalite is.<br /><br />But rough. Such a rough and dark book in so many ways. Oh, this series; still so powerful even after all these years.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9331622069295415887">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1201724314">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1201724314" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/12904304-alan-gilfoy" class="left imgcol" title="Alan Gilfoy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1347886916p2/12904304.jpg" alt="Alan Gilfoy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1201724314?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 15, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12904304-alan-gilfoy" class="user" title="Alan Gilfoy">Alan Gilfoy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1201724314">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13335791940621923946">Tobias' hawk issues sure sure showed up quickly, but slightly differently than his usual angst. It's clear he's fawning over Rachel - can't blame him for that. It makes sense that the species barrier would get to them, that Rachel wants some normalcy. "She's not all warrior" seems like a nod to the split personality of the last book.<br /><br />It looks like Erek is creating a diversion for them, or he came to tell the Animorphs something and needed to come up with a distraction for himself.<br /><br />There was great</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13335791940621923946">Tobias' hawk issues sure sure showed up quickly, but slightly differently than his usual angst. It's clear he's fawning over Rachel - can't blame him for that. It makes sense that the species barrier would get to them, that Rachel wants some normalcy. "She's not all warrior" seems like a nod to the split personality of the last book.<br /><br />It looks like Erek is creating a diversion for them, or he came to tell the Animorphs something and needed to come up with a distraction for himself.<br /><br />There was great planning for the bait mission. I liked the change of pace in confusing the Yeerks about their plan versus sabotaging the device or event itself. Responsible leader Jake and brave Rachel - it makes sense that they'd volunteer first, though Ax is better for the mission and Tobias is much better. I sort of saw that choice coming.<br /><br />It's about time one of them morphed an Andalite - even though they couldn't make it a habit (showing the Yeerks a bunch of clones), I thought that would have happened a bit already. Tobias trying out the morph was great for the Tobias-Ax relationship as well as providing canon on Andalites.<br /><br />How do the Yeerks understand morphing technology well enough to reverse it?<br /><br />The action flowed well. I was surprised that the eagle wasn't Rachel, but instead an actual injured bird. Well, it was terminal anyway.<br /><br />Ah, so losing Tobias is one of the few things Rachel is afraid of. Tobias didn't seem to want Taylor dead, with "let Visser Three torture her" as an argument that would resonate with Rachel. The Taylor-Rachel comparison told me that "popular girl falling from grace" was another path Rachel's life could have taken. This seems similar to how Tobias could've been susceptible to the Sharing if he didn't have Jake looking out for him.<br /><br />Tobias' torture was more great background on his messed-up life. His uncle was gratuitously mean about the art, but I don't understand the neighbor kid getting praised for crap either. Tobias' uncle zoned out in front of the TV reminds me of Marco's father after Eva's supposed death. The choppy prose seemed symbolic of the pressure Tobias was under. I've often heard of writers doing that and this is one of the first times I've noticed it.<br /><br />Often Animorphs blends plot and comic relief. This book combined current action and facts about the setting similarly well.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13335791940621923946">...more</a>

After some confusion with Rachel suggesting she wants Tobias to be human, the team has to go after the Anti-Morphing Ray and Tobias volunteers himself as the one to be captured, because if they use the ray on him he won't turn into a human and they'll think the ray doesn't work. He meets Taylor, a human-Controller with an insane past, and while he's tortured with memories both painful and pleasurable, he also has visions of his Andalite father. I pity your innocence."<br />Tobias: "What would you know about disloyalty?"<br /><br />Tobias: "You've failed him. Visser Three won't tolerate failure. You know that. But I guess that's life in the happy little Yeerk Empire. I won't give in. Do you know why?"<br />Taylor: "No."<br />Tobias: "Because if I surrender, you'll live. And if I resist, you'll die. And I want you to die." </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4262257667381434151">This one was difficult for me to read as a child, mostly because of the torture scenes. It's dark and frightening and probably one of the realest books in the series thus far (as real as a series about alien brain invaders can be anyway). This time around it was still difficult to read, but only when things started to get all trippy with Tobias remembering Elfangor's memories. And then Ax's explanation set me over the top. As I said when I watched that one really stupid episode of <em>Enterprise</em> (as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4262257667381434151">This one was difficult for me to read as a child, mostly because of the torture scenes. It's dark and frightening and probably one of the realest books in the series thus far (as real as a series about alien brain invaders can be anyway). This time around it was still difficult to read, but only when things started to get all trippy with Tobias remembering Elfangor's memories. And then Ax's explanation set me over the top. As I said when I watched that one really stupid episode of <em>Enterprise</em> (as if there's only one, lbr): MEMORIES ARE NOT STORED IN DNA AND CANNOT BE TRANSMITTED THUS.<br /><br />Also I guess I'm kinda seeing less and less of any sort of emotional connection between Rachel and Tobias? Which is a huge disappointment considering I rooted for them so hard as a kid. But reading them as an adult, they don't feel as ~destined~ as I once felt them to be. Rachel basically just whines all the time about how Tobias is unwilling to commit to being 100% human and how this totally sucks for her, and Tobias seems to be hung up on Rachel's beauty. He kind of acknowledges her self-destructive tendencies, but he's more likely than any of the others to ignore them or even admire her for them. They're basically super dysfunctional, and not just in the "Romeo and Juliet" way they keep referencing.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_965985822">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/965985822" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11346136-katelynn" class="left imgcol" title="Katelynn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442287962p2/11346136.jpg" alt="Katelynn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/965985822?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 13, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11346136-katelynn" class="user" title="Katelynn">Katelynn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11346136-katelynn?shelf=favourite-books" class="actionLinkLite">favourite-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11346136-katelynn?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer965985822">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10338680467020469652">Okay I need to get serious for a second. This book exploded me. Any emotional damage I have as an adult is PROBABLY FROM READING THIS AS A TWELVE YEAR OLD (thanks mom) (but seriously, thanks mom). I wonder if this book - my favourite from the regular series, a book I read so often I carried it with me everywhere and eventually lost it - is how I came to love the things I love. How all pain has a root that I love to unearth; how pleasure can hurt more than anything, how the memory of it is what m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10338680467020469652">Okay I need to get serious for a second. This book exploded me. Any emotional damage I have as an adult is PROBABLY FROM READING THIS AS A TWELVE YEAR OLD (thanks mom) (but seriously, thanks mom). I wonder if this book - my favourite from the regular series, a book I read so often I carried it with me everywhere and eventually lost it - is how I came to love the things I love. How all pain has a root that I love to unearth; how pleasure can hurt more than anything, how the memory of it is what makes you want to die in the end. And how everything can be made okay by that brave, golden love of your life, walking over the sand on the beach to meet you after it's all over. That's my writing in a nutshell. And that's this book in a nutshell. This book, hands down, is the reason that, 15 years later, I still can't forget everything these kids went through. And I think I became a better kid from sticking it through with them, too.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10338680467020469652">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/909797657?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 14, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4686247-priscilla" class="user" title="Priscilla">Priscilla</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer909797657">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18236141844174425325">In effort to find and destroy the anti-morphing ray that the Yeerks are developing, the Animorphs need to prove the ray doesn't work. The only one who can carry out the plan is Tobias, but as always, it's a dangerous plan.<br /><br />I change my mind about who my favourite Animorph is every other book, but Tobias' background is my favourite subplot. We get glimpses of that here, with memories of his uncaring guardians and the scenes of him and Ax practicing an Andalite's ritual. Tobias doesn't quite fit any</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18236141844174425325">In effort to find and destroy the anti-morphing ray that the Yeerks are developing, the Animorphs need to prove the ray doesn't work. The only one who can carry out the plan is Tobias, but as always, it's a dangerous plan.<br /><br />I change my mind about who my favourite Animorph is every other book, but Tobias' background is my favourite subplot. We get glimpses of that here, with memories of his uncaring guardians and the scenes of him and Ax practicing an Andalite's ritual. Tobias doesn't quite fit anywhere - he's a hawk and a boy and also descended from an Andalite but isn't actually one - and he's grown up with no one wanting him, and that came through strongly in this book. <br /><br />Without going into details, the part where Tobias is captured is quite intense and I was simultaneously fascinated and horrified. Once again I'm reminded that, aliens aside, this is a series about a war.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18236141844174425325">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span id="like_container_review_909797657" class="likeItContainer"><a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F302871.The_Illusion" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" rel="nofollow">Like</a></span> · <a href="/review/show/909797657?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1">see review</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1244772839">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1244772839" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5975841-stephanie" class="left imgcol" title="Stephanie"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Stephanie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1244772839?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5975841-stephanie" class="user" title="Stephanie">Stephanie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5975841-stephanie?shelf=childhood-memories" class="actionLinkLite">childhood-memories</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5975841-stephanie?shelf=animorphs" class="actionLinkLite">animorphs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1244772839">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1176752173240893338">This book was so incredibly difficult to read. Usually, I have a hard time slowing down as I read these. Not this one. No, this one I could not <em>not</em> read slowly. It hurt to read, and not for any deficiency in the writing or the story. It hurt to read because of what happens, what Tobias suffers on this mission. If we thought he had already suffered and lost enough – getting trapped as a red-tailed hawk, having to survive as a hawk, gaining back his morphing ability but staying a hawk, learning ab</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1176752173240893338">   This book was so incredibly difficult to read. Usually, I have a hard time slowing down as I read these. Not this one. No, this one I could not <em>not</em> read slowly. It hurt to read, and not for any deficiency in the writing or the story. It hurt to read because of what happens, what Tobias suffers on this mission. If we thought he had already suffered and lost enough – getting trapped as a red-tailed hawk, having to survive as a hawk, gaining back his morphing ability but staying a hawk, learning about who his father is, falling in love with Rachel despite now being different species – that was just the internal suffering. That was just his characterization and personal development.<br /><br />   To backtrack to the happy side, though, there are some very touching moments between Tobias and Rachel at the school dance. And a very good “family” moment between Ax and Tobias in the woods. Those are the lights on either side of this dark tunnel of a book.<br /><br />   <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[“The dark tunnel” is the war that is here and how close to Tobias it strikes. Now comes the physical suffering, the pain that comes from being in a war. The pain that cuts deep into the soul as it cuts into your body. The pain that can break you as nothing else can. He was emotionally and psychologically scarred before, but now he is physically and even more psychologically scarred after the trials he undergoes in this book. If he wasn’t a part of the Animorphs PTSD-support group before, he will definitely be now. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />       <strong>Out of respect for life, you must endure.</strong><br /><br />   Quotes and comments – I typed up and commented on the first 92 pages before finishing the book, so the ideas/tone behind the comments will reflect that break.<br /><br />   We’d been through this before [Rachel and I]. I didn’t know how to answer. And I didn’t know why she was pushing it.<br />   Ever since I overstayed the two-hour time limit in morph I’ve considered hawk to be my true form. Hawk is the body I have to keep if I want to help the other Animorphs and Ax combat the Yeerk invasion. Why was Rachel ignoring reality? She knew as well as anyone that I’d be out of the fight if I stayed more than two hours in human form. – page 5 – Tobias really is more about the team than the individual, isn’t he? I think Rachel is ignoring reality at this dance, and all the time, because if Tobias were to stay human, she would have a reason to “stay human” as well. Even though he’s a bird, he grounds her. He keeps her human.<br /><br />   “Tobias, I want to explain…” [Rachel] broke off as her eyes followed mine to the picture of the red-tailed hawk and the caption beneath it. “Longevity in the wild,” it read. “Almost never reaches the figures attained by captive birds guarded against disease and predation. A generous estimate: eighteen years.”<br />   Rachel stared at the wall. I looked at the floor. In an instant, the bulletin board display had thrown our friendship into the harsh light of reality. Rachel was a girl who could, on occasion, become a bird of prey. I was a hawk who could, on occasion, become human. – page 9 – Ouch. Not just the harsh reality of their friendship, but also any possible relationship they might have/develop. And the harsh reality of their own lives as human and hawk.<br /><br />   The clock was ticking down and I wasn’t even sure Rachel was on my side.<br />   In minutes I’d be trapped. Trapped as a person who was no longer me. – page 13 – That’s probably the hardest thing for Tobias – he no longer considers himself human, and doesn’t want to go back to it. As we’ve seen through his books, he has truly and completely embraced who he is as a Bird-boy. To become anything else would be to sacrifice himself needlessly.<br /><br />   [Jake said,] “I’m glad you made it, Tobias. You’re our eyes. Our ears. Our air force. If we lost you we’d be nothing. Like Joan of Arc without her sword. Patton without his pearl-handled pistols…”<br />   /[…] Stop the flattery, man. You’re making me blush./ We both laughed. It felt good to hear Jake say I was indispensable. But with Jake you could never be sure anymore what was sincere. And what was just expedient.<br />   He’d been the most open of guys, back in the old days. What you saw with Jake was what you got. But he’d been a leader for a long time now. He’d learned to say what he needed to say.<br />   Jake needed me as one of the Animorphs. He liked me, respected me, was happy for me when I was happy. And, when he had to, he used me without regards for anything but winning. – page 19-20 – We are seeing a lot more of Jake through the eyes of others lately, aren’t we? And they are all seeing the same thing: a leader who says what needs to be said, and does what needs to be done, in order to win. <br /><br />   /Been boning up on famous leaders, haven’t you?/<br />   “A little, yeah. Don’t tell anyone, though. I want my brilliance to appear unstudied. Natural.” Jake smiled up at me and gave a quick salute. “Later, Red Baron.” – page 20<br /><br />   /Tobias,/ Ax said as he reached the clearing,/ this is a special moment, is it not?/<br />   /How do you mean?/ I answered carefully.<br />   /Well, you are…/ Ax hesitated in an uncharacteristic way. /I mean, we are related, are we not? You are not Andalite, exactly, but you carry the Andalite heritage. I am glad you will have that DNA in you from now on. It is a very unique genetic mixture./<br />   /Oh, we all know how much you think of your species, Ax,/ I kidded.<br />   /I do hold Andalites in very high regards. It is true. But it isn’t an unthinking allegiance. I honestly admire my culture. There are things I would like to teach you, to share with you if you are interested./<br />   If I was interested! I wanted so much to stay cool. To make it seem like I could take it or leave it. But this was something, finally, that I really did have a right to. I was part Andalite, even if not genetically. God knew how. Or at least [t]he Ellimist knew how. But I was. And it excited me. – page 32-33 – And now, it is time for a touching Ax and Tobias family moment. As much as the Animorphs are Tobias’ family, this is blood/ancestral family, something that until now, was never a valuable nor important thing in his life.<br /><br />   [Tobias struck the tree with his tail] FWAPP!<br />   /Ahhh! Oh! Ouch! Ax?!/<br />   /Yes, Tobias. You have impaled the tree with the tip of your blade. That is not the desired result./<br />   /Yeah, I sorta guessed that./<br />   I yanked and twisted. I couldn’t free my blade.<br />   /You struck with impressive velocity,/ Ax observed. /That, at least, is admirable./ -- page 36-37 – Haha. Nice job, Ax, just have Tobias plunge right into all this, hm?<br /><br />   /Tobias?/ [Rachel] said softly in private thought-speak.<br />   /What is it? Do you want out?/<br />   /No, of course not. It’s not that./ She paused. /Listen. Um. You take care of yourself. I mean…be careful. Okay? Whatever happens? If it comes down to it, save yourself and forget the stupid mission./<br />   I smiled inwardly. She was concerned about me. If I had been human… looking into Rachel’s eyes, feeling her next to me, I might have… But she was a fly on my hawk body. Which was good. I could keep my cool. A hawk’s feelings aren’t exactly visible to others.<br />   /I will,/ I said simply. Then added, /I have a lot to lose. / -- page 63-64 – I’m honestly surprised that Rachel would stay with Tobias on this mission – I would think it would have been considered too dangerous to have more than just Tobias caught. Plus she’s running low on morph time (already over an hour gone), if something should happen.<br /><br />   <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[It was crazy! Inconceivable arrogance on our parts. We had underestimated our foe. A fatal error.<br />   Fatal.<br />   The hawk brain, the animal part that still, even now, lived apart from me, untouched by human reason, began a low, defeated moan. A death moan. – page 77 – The Animorphs do rely rather heavily on luck, don’t they? This is a hard wake-up call.<br /><br />   We had met many times, [Visser Three] and I. But visible through those Andalite eyes was an evil that still struck fear in my heart. Still gripped me with hopelessness and despair.<br />   Perhaps it was the knowledge that this Yeerk had managed something that years of battle had been unable to do: take down the great Elfangor. Stamp out that brave warrior’s life. Or maybe looking into Visser Three’s eyes made me face the hard reality that despite all our campaigns – the numerous ways we’ve succeeded in weakening and slowing his invasion of Earth – this Yeerk still stood powerful and strong.<br />   Was he just lucky? Or was he really smarter than we were?<br />   Would he always triumph? Would we never be able to end the invasion? To change the course of humanity’s future? – page 82 – This is some of the most straight-forwardly pessimistic thinking we’ve had from Tobias or any of the others, I think. Visser Three has been very lucky, just like the Animorphs have been, that’s for sure. Also, it’s natural to feel fearful and doubtful when you are trapped. We’re getting the first taste of what it is like to be captured and tortured by the enemy. I’m sad that it has to be Tobias who has to suffer this, though…it makes this book hard to read.<br /><br />   Inside, [the sub-visser “Taylor”] and Rachel were like night and day.<br />   Or at least night and twilight. – page 90 – Tobias knows Rachel. And three-pointer for additional foreshadowing on Rachel’s character development.<br /><br />   Me, the human me, the boy inside kept screaming, tell her, tell her!<br />   But the hawk…the hawk suffered dumb, helpless. The hawk had no way out. The me that was a bird, the body, the physical me didn’t know that there was a cause for the pain.<br />   Didn’t know it could make the pain end. And already, for the hawk, the pain had become a fact of life. Reality.<br />   Life was hunger. Life was killing. Life was danger. Life was pain.<br />   The hawk could manage it. Not on a conscious level, of course, but by shutting down. Keeping alive on a sort of primitive autopilot. Only essential parts of the organism were maintained. No contemplation. No decision. Not even observation. Just survival.<br />   The boy Tobias screamed.<br />   The hawk Tobias had already begun to accept the pain. – page 92-93 – Marco was spot on when he said that when things get hard, Tobias retreats more and more into his hawk self. We see it here, and I have a feeling we’ll continue to see it as this book unfolds.<br /><br />--- commented the above before continued reading ---<br /><br />   [Tobias is having flashes of memory real and composited while being tortured – these flashes are all in italics in the book too]<br />   <em>In truth, nothing but a mask – a morph – for Visser Three. Visser Three, plotting my death.</em><br />   <em>I was a dupe. Again.</em><br />   <em>False hope.</em><br />   <em>Never trust... never!</em> -- page 100 – These scenes are his worst nightmares come alive. They are his fears and weaknesses chewing at him from the inside as he is being physically tortured.<br /><br />   <em>Elfangor. The father I never knew. My link to everything strong, enduring, and good in the universe.</em><br />   <em>Murdered.</em><br />   <em>Anger boiled inside me. A rage whose power made me shake. Energy that rose up and took control. Infested me. I will end him! I will end that Yeerk! The hatred carved away my insides. Scarred me, scraped me clean.</em><br />   <em>Leave me free! I pleaded. But the anger wouldn’t go.</em> -- page 103 – For Tobias, anger is an alien thing. It’s not something that is a part of him… until now, it seems.<br /><br />   <em>And as I flew, I felt the burden of a thousand wounds, each one fresh and vivid in my mind. Weighing me down.</em><br />   <em>How can you carry such a weight? All the pain I had inflicted. Seemingly inevitable. Perhaps avoidable. Strikes made by me. A hawk. A warrior. A ruthless kid.</em> -- page 104 – If I’m not mistaken, I think this is the first time Tobias has referred to himself as ruthless outside of his actions as a hawk for pure survival.<br /><br />   “Time’s almost up, Andalite. You’ll never run free again. Never use that fantastic tail of yours. You’ll die, so soon. How long does a hawk live?” [sub-visser Taylor taunted.]<br />   <em>Rachel?</em><br />   <em>No, no, the sub-visser.</em><br />   <em>I want you with me, to be part of me, my life, not to die a bird, not to die for nothing.</em><br />   <em>Rachel?</em><br />   <em>Rachel! Rachel! </em> -- page 110 – As Tobias is Rachel’s lifeline to keeping her humanity, she too, is Tobias’ lifeline for survival.<br /><br />   “Your childish loyalty is amusing. But you’ll learn, Andalite.” [The sub-visser] spoke the words bitterly and with emphasis. “You’ll learn that it’s foolish to protect your friends. Friends always betray you.”<br />   I answered instinctively, forgetting to keep up my guard. /Mine wouldn’t./<br />   “Oh, wouldn’t they?” she snapped. […] I could tell she had more to say, but she bottled it, and said simply, “I pity your innocence.” – page 115 – I’m glad Tobias is confident in his friends despite what he has gone through. It’s a good illustration of just how important the other Animorphs and Ax are to him.<br /><br />   [The sub-visser explained her host’s story, and how she wanted to be envied again like her host was as a beautiful, popular girl at school before the fire.] “I wanted all of that, all the memories, the sweet, perfect memories, I wanted to live that life.”<br />   <em>She’s crazy,</em> I realized. <em>She’s insane. The Yeerk. The girl. The line between them all confused.<br />   Hawk. Boy.<br />   Yeerk. Girl.</em><br />   I had a terrible moment of understanding. – page 121 – As powerful as this line is, I thought he already understood. I thought that this confusion of self he has was resolved long ago.<br /><br />   <em>/You’re not alone in your suffering. You may die, Tobias, but never alone. You are one in a legion of great warriors. Valiant Andalites who have died for freedom. Your lineage is courage and bravery. If you live, you carry our torch. A burden carried by many. A singular honor…/</em> […]<br />   The last, fading strain of Elfangor’s voice:<br />   <em>/Out of respect for life, you have to endure./</em> -- page 131<br /><br />   [The cavalry has arrived to free Tobias at last]<br />   For a split second, time froze. And I saw Rachel and Taylor face-to-face. One strong. Her morph a crazy manifestation of an inner strength and bravery. One weak. This girl for whom appearance had been everything, honor nothing. This poor girl whose weakness had made her easy prey for the Yeerks. And I felt pity. Pity for my torturer.<br />   Rachel’s claws closed on Taylor’s neck. Crushing her esophagus. She was turning blue, suffocating.<br />   “Help!” she rasped pitifully. “Someone help me!”<br />   /Rachel! No. Rachel, don’t do it!/<br />   /She dies, Tobias. For what she did to you, she dies./ She moved as if to slam Taylor against the wall.<br />   /No!/ I yelled. /Rachel. No./<br />   Rachel turned to look at me. Hesitated. Then dropped Taylor like a crumpled candy wrapper. […]<br />   /You know she should die, Tobias,/ Rachel said.<br />   /She will,/ I said. /This is the Yeerk who lost a prisoner. Leave her to Visser Three./<br />   /What she did to you…/<br />   /Rachel. Be Rachel, not her./ -- page 150-151 – First off, this is a strong reminder of Tobias’ humanity. Though he retreats into his hawk self to survive, it his his humanity which will ultimately carry him through. This is also a powerful illustration of how Tobias is the one who can bring Rachel back from the brink. He is possibly the <em>only</em> one who can save her from herself. If he were to die, I don’t think Rachel would survive either – she would lose herself utterly.<br /><br />   Can I just pretend that the last few lines of the book never happened? They’re such a step backwards. It may be that they’re a coping mechanism – easier to realize that the answer to what/who Tobias is isn’t a single word or moment than to deal with the physical and psychological torture –but it feels like a cop-out to me. “It could take a lifetime to figure out who I am.” – well, he already <em>knew</em> that, as did we. It was tempting to knock my rating down by a star for this clearly backwards step, but I resisted. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_32696127">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/32696127" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/84660-swankivy" class="left imgcol" title="Swankivy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1220079335p2/84660.jpg" alt="Swankivy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/32696127?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 06, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/84660-swankivy" class="user" title="Swankivy">Swankivy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer32696127">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7713601244195350600">A trap over an anti-morphing ray gets Tobias in a bind--he gets very graphically tortured by a human-Controller. Scary.<br /><br />Notable moments and inconsistencies:<br /><br />This book is ghostwritten by Ellen Geroux.<br /><br />In this book Jake admits to having begun to study famous leaders, but jokes that no one should let on because he wants his brilliance to seem unstudied.<br /><br />Cassie makes an excuse about not being able to go to The Sharing meeting because she says her parents will notice her missing and would worry. Neverthe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7713601244195350600">A trap over an anti-morphing ray gets Tobias in a bind--he gets very graphically tortured by a human-Controller. Scary.<br /><br />Notable moments and inconsistencies:<br /><br />This book is ghostwritten by Ellen Geroux.<br /><br />In this book Jake admits to having begun to study famous leaders, but jokes that no one should let on because he wants his brilliance to seem unstudied.<br /><br />Cassie makes an excuse about not being able to go to The Sharing meeting because she says her parents will notice her missing and would worry. Nevertheless, she is part of the mission, with no commentary. By this point it's common for them to get the Chee to pose as them when they need to be at a mission, but this setup was never discussed.<br /><br />Tobias is the first of the Animorphs to morph an Andalite, and he points out through his experience that Andalites have an instinct for optimism.<br /><br />Visser Three's thought-speak voice is said to strike Tobias's ear. Seems like a poor description since thought-speak doesn't use ears.<br /><br />Taylor hits Tobias with her fake arm at one point, and he notes that it's her right arm. But later in the book Taylor is spilling out her experiences about how she lost her limbs and got burned, and she refers to having "lost her left arm." She's only supposed to have one false arm so it's unclear which one is "really" artificial.<br /><br />There are several thought-speaking glitches when Visser Three and Tobias are both talking in thought-speak; two of Taylor's spoken lines are framed in thought-speak as well, but this is a mistake.<br /><br />While Tobias is experiencing Elfangor's memories, several phrases are used to describe his experiences which sound like things humans would say, such as "making a retching noise" (Andalites don't have mouths, so they can't "retch"), "expelling" breakfast (they can't vomit) and experiencing "nausea" (which seems like an odd way to describe it if they can't vomit). </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7713601244195350600">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer670576232">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14051057091895286715"><img width="300" height="150" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404645r/787607._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /><strong>Brought to you by <a rel="nofollow" href="http://moonlightlibrary.wordpress.com/projectanimorphs/">The Moonlight Library</a>!</strong><br /><br />Tobias and the Animorphs need to stop the Yeerks’ newest invention: the anti-morphing ray. This means one of the Animorphs needs to ‘prove’ it doesn’t work. The only one who can do that is Tobias – his nothlit body is a hawk, so any forced ‘demorph’ would fail.<br /><br />This book is one of the most harrowing in the series. Not only does the darkness stem from Tobias’ own sad home life, but it features torture by an insane Controller and the most incredible and gory</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14051057091895286715"><img width="300" height="150" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404645r/787607._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /><strong>Brought to you by <a rel="nofollow" href="http://moonlightlibrary.wordpress.com/projectanimorphs/">The Moonlight Library</a>!</strong><br /><br />Tobias and the Animorphs need to stop the Yeerks’ newest invention: the anti-morphing ray. This means one of the Animorphs needs to ‘prove’ it doesn’t work. The only one who can do that is Tobias – his nothlit body is a hawk, so any forced ‘demorph’ would fail.<br /><br />This book is one of the most harrowing in the series. Not only does the darkness stem from Tobias’ own sad home life, but it features torture by an insane Controller and the most incredible and gory fight scene written into the Animorphs series. In short, it’s awesome J<br /><br />Tobias isn’t ‘captured’ until about halfway through the book, and before that we get a lovely scene where he needs to practice morphing Ax (so he still has an ‘Andalite’ morph). Tobias and Ax are related, in a weird way. This scene makes me smile and breaks my heart a little. Ax may be millions of miles away from his home world and people, but Tobias is his nephew and Ax wants to share his culture with the strange, broken human boy.<br /><br />Similarly, as Tobias slowly moves towards death, he experiences a strange Andalite fable called utzum, one that Ax does not entirely believe in. I’ve always loved the romantic idea of Tobias being part Andalite, but when you look at it really, morphing is all about DNA. He actually has no part of Andalite in him at all, not even the human part of him. He would have inherited some stranger’s genes (Elfangor’s human morph) along with his mother’s, so I’ve never really understood how he can experience Andalite things such as Ax’s cry for help in Book #4, or this utzum.<br /><br />Of course, when you love Tobias and are watching him be tortured to death, you can suspend your disbelief, ignore the plot holes, and focus on how Elfangor is his daddy and Tobias is actually the son of the greatest Andalite hero ever. And that’s how he’s strong enough to not only withstand the torture, but to let his torturer go when the other Animorphs finally show up to rescue him and Rachl puts two and two together and understandably flies into a rage in grizzly morph.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14051057091895286715">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6361932549978122685">This is one of the most epic books in the series, especially if you're a Rachel and Tobias shipper (what is the official name for that, anyway? I never bothered to look it up officially, if there is one). This was obviously ghost written, and yet, the writer seems to be a bit more talented than Applegate herself! We really get to delve into Tobais' mind from a more realistic, perhaps "adult" standpoint. Keep in mind that time has passed since the first book. They were supposed to be 13 in the fi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6361932549978122685">This is one of the most epic books in the series, especially if you're a Rachel and Tobias shipper (what is the official name for that, anyway? I never bothered to look it up officially, if there is one). This was obviously ghost written, and yet, the writer seems to be a bit more talented than Applegate herself! We really get to delve into Tobais' mind from a more realistic, perhaps "adult" standpoint. Keep in mind that time has passed since the first book. They were supposed to be 13 in the first book, so they're about 14 or 15 here. There's an awesome scene at the end where Tobias and Rachel kiss, which is awesome... The whole introduction of the sub-visser is really interesting. This is one of the books in the series that is truly difficult to put down. Oh, and Tobias even gets to acquire Ax! Yeah, this book truly shows us how far we've come sine the first book. I highly recommend this one.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('isDil6LKBD9Hz+brr+xoScGZKFAqZ07farRYwXcBBHfvFN1EUBgQxcsXklDRjY77iG7rSWO6CXUAvV1Tu5TyMg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('f/rn9jhZWzKPLiosgQanoNQnEQvPoTkt6tkA85PaWskaLtglyotPyAP2Xpf/Z0ESndDSEoZ8foeA0AVhX0+sjA==')})
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1036736.Katherine_Applegate">About Katherine Applegate</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1036736.Katherine_Applegate"><img alt="1036736" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1269837168p2/1036736.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer898351276566891545">Applegate was born in Michigan in 1956. Since then she has lived in Texas, Florida, California, Minnesota, Illinois, North Carolina, and after living in Pelago, Italy for a year, she has moved back to Southern California. She has an eleven year old son named Jake Mates, although she says the Animorph leader is not named after him. In 2003 she and her husband, Michael Grant, her co-author on many p</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText898351276566891545">Applegate was born in Michigan in 1956. Since then she has lived in Texas, Florida, California, Minnesota, Illinois, North Carolina, and after living in Pelago, Italy for a year, she has moved back to Southern California. She has an eleven year old son named Jake Mates, although she says the Animorph leader is not named after him. In 2003 she and her husband, Michael Grant, her co-author on many projects including Animorphs, adopted their daughter, Julia, in China.[citation needed] Following the end of Animorphs, Applegate took three years off. She is back at work and has written a picture book called "The Buffalo Storm," a middle reader novel called "Home of the Brave," and an early chapters series "Roscoe Riley Rules" with Harper Collins. Her book "Home of the Brave" has won the SCBWI Golden Kite Award, the Bank Street 2008 Josette Frank Award, and is a Judy Lopez Memorial Award honor book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="898351276566891545">...more</a>

    </div>
